"I? I see myself holding a pair of thick, woolen socks." Roberto stared.
"One can never have enough socks," said Dominguez. "Another Christmas has come and gone and I didn't get a single pair. People will insist on giving me books."
171
It was only when he was back in bed that it struck Roberto that Dominguez might not have been quite truthful. But then, he thought, as he shoved Scabbers off his pillow, it had been quite a personal question.
CHAPTER THIRTEEN NICOLAS FLAMEL
Dominguez had convinced Roberto not to go looking for the Mirror of Erised again, and for the rest of the Christmas holidays the
invisibility cloak stayed folded at the bottom of his trunk. Roberto
wished he could forget what he'd seen in the mirror as easily, but he couldn't. He started having nightmares. Over and over again he dreamed about his parents disappearing in a flash of green light, while a high voice cackled with laughter.
"You see, Dominguez was right, that mirror could drive you mad," said Diego, when Roberto told him about these drearns.
Carolina, who came back the day before term started, took a different view of things. She was torn between horror at the idea of Roberto being out of bed, roaming the school three nights in a row ("If Filch had caught you!"), and disappointment that he hadn't at least found out who Nicolas Flamel was.
They had almost given up hope of ever finding Flamel in a li- brary book, even though Roberto was still sure he'd read the name somewhere. Once term had started, they were back to skimming through books for ten minutes during their breaks. Roberto had even less time than the other
two, because Quidditch practice had started again.
Wood was working the team harder than ever. Even the endless rain that had replaced the snow couldn't dampen his spirits. The Lopezs complained that Wood was becoming a fanatic, but Roberto was on Wood's side. If they won their next match, against Hufflepuff, they would overtake Slytherin in the house championship for the first time in seven years. Quite apart from wanting to win, Roberto found that he had fewer nightmares when he was tired out after training.
Then, during one particularly wet and muddy practice session, Wood gave the team a bit of bad news. He'd just gotten very angry with the
172
Lopezs, who kept dive-bombing each other and pretending to fall off their brooms.
"Will you stop messing around!" he yelled. "That's exactly the sort of thing that'll lose us the match! Peralta's refereeing this time, and he'll be looking for any excuse to knock points off Gryffindor!"
Luis Lopez really did fall off his broom at these words.
"Peralta's refereeing?" he spluttered through a mouthful of mud. "When's he ever refereed a Quidditch match? He's not going to be fair if we might overtake Slytherin."
The rest of the team landed next to Luis to complain, too.
"It's not my fault," said Wood. "We've just got to make sure we play a clean game, so Peralta hasn't got an excuse to pick on us."
Which was all very well, thought Roberto, but he had another reason for not wanting Peralta near him while he was playing Quidditch....
The rest of the team hung back to talk to one another as usual at the
end of practice, but Roberto headed straight back to the Gryffindor common room, where he found Diego and Carolina playing chess. Chess was the only thing Carolina ever lost at, something Roberto and Diego thought was very good for her.
"Don't talk to me for a moment," said Diego when Roberto sat down next to him, "I need to concen --" He caught sight of Roberto's face. "What's the matter with you? You look terrible."
Speaking quietly so that no one else would hear, Roberto told the other two about Peralta's sudden, sinister desire to be a Quidditch referee.
"Don't play," said Carolina at once.
"Say you're ill," said Diego.
"Pretend to break your leg," Carolina suggested.

The next morning in Defense Against the Dark Arts, while copying down different ways of treating werewolf bites, Roberto and Diego were still discussing what they'd do with a Sorcerer's Stone if they had one. It wasn't until Diego said he'd buy his own Quidditch team that Roberto remembered about Peralta and the coming match.

As the match drew nearer, however, Roberto became more and more nervous, whatever he told Diego and Carolina. The rest of the team wasn't too calm, either. The idea of overtaking Slytherin in the house championship was wonderful, no one had done it for seven years, but would they be allowed to, with such a biased referee?
Roberto didn't know whether he was imagining it or not, but he seemed to keep running into Peralta wherever he went. At times, he even wondered whether Peralta was following him, trying to catch him on his own. Potions

lessons were turning into a sort of weekly torture, Peralta was so

Roberto had reached the shed. He leaned against the wooden door and looked up at Hogwarts, with its windows glowing red in the setting sun. Gryffindor in the lead. He'd done it, he'd shown Peralta....
And speaking of Peralta...
A hooded figure came swiftly down the front steps of the castle. Clearly not wanting to be seen, it walked as fast as possible toward the forbidden forest. Roberto's victory faded from his mind as he watched. He recognized the figure's prowling walk. Peralta, sneaking into the forest while everyone else was at dinner -- what was going on?
Roberto jumped back on his Nimbus Two Thousand and took off. Gliding silently over the castle he saw Peralta enter the forest at a run. He followed.

heard voices. He glided toward them and landed noiselessly in a towering beech tree.

CHAPTER FOURTEEN
NORBERT THE NORWEGIAN RIDGEBACK
Quirrell, however, must have been braver than they'd thought. In the weeks that followed he did seem to be getting paler and thinner, but it didn't look as though he'd cracked yet.
Every time they passed the third-floor corridor, Roberto, Diego, and Carolina would press their ears to the door to check that Fluffy was still growling inside. Peralta was sweeping about in his usual bad temper, which surely meant that the Stone was still safe. Whenever Roberto passed Quirrell these days he gave him an encouraging sort of smile, and Diego had started telling people off for laughing at Quirrell's stutter.
Carolina, however, had more on her mind than the Sorcerer's Stone. She had started drawing up study schedules and colorcoding all her notes. Roberto and Diego wouldn't have minded, but she kept nagging them to do the same.
"Carolina, the exams are ages away."
"Ten weeks," Carolina snapped. "That's not ages, that's like a second to Nicolas Flamel."
"But we're not six hundred years old," Diego reminded her. "Anyway, what are you studying for, you already know it A."
"What am I studying for? Are you crazy? You realize we need to pass these exams to get into the second year? They're very important, I should have started studying a month ago, I don't know what's gotten into me...."
182
Unfortunately, the teachers seemed to be thinking along the same lines
as Carolina. They piled so much homework on them that the Easter holidays weren't nearly as much fun as the Christmas ones. It was hard
to relax with Carolina next to you reciting the twelve uses of dragon's blood or practicing wand movements. Moaning and yawning, Roberto and Diego spent most of their free time in the library with her, trying to get
through all their extra work.
"I'll never remember this," Diego burst out one afternoon, throwing down his quill and looking longingly out of the library window. It was the
first really fine day they'd had in months. The sky was a clear, forget-me-not blue, and there was a feeling in the air of summer coming.
Roberto, who was looking up "Dittany" in One Thousand Magical Herbs and Fungi, didn't look up until he heard Diego say, "Villalba! What are you
doing in the library?"
Villalba shuffled into view, hiding something behind his back. He looked very out of place in his moleskin overcoat.
"Jus' lookin'," he said, in a shifty voice that got their interest at
once. "An' what're you lot up ter?" He looked suddenly suspicious. "Yer not still lookin' fer Nicolas Flamel, are yeh?" "Oh, we found out who he is ages ago," said Diego impressively. "And we know what that dog's guarding, it's a Sorcerer's St --"
"Shhhh!" Villalba looked around quickly to see if anyone was listening. "Don' go shoutin' about it, what's the matter with yeh?"
"There are a few things we wanted to ask you, as a matter of fact," said Roberto, "about what's guarding the Stone apart from Fluffy --"
"SHHHH!" said Villalba again. "Listen - come an' see me later, I'm not promisin' I'll tell yeh anythin', mind, but don' go rabbitin' about it
in here, students aren' s'pposed ter know. They'll think I've told yeh --"

"What was he hiding behind his back?" said Carolina thoughtfully.

"Do you think it had anything to do with the Stone?"

"Villalba's always wanted a dragon, he told me so the first time I ever met him, " said Roberto.
"But it's against our laws," said Diego. "Dragon breeding was outlawed by the Warlocks' Convention of 1709, everyone knows that. It's hard to stop Muggles from noticing us if we're keeping dragons in the back garden - anyway, you can't tame dragons, it's dangerous. You should see the burns Charlie's got off wild ones in Romania."
"But there aren't wild dragons in Britain?" said Roberto.
"Of course there are," said Diego. "Common Welsh Green and Hebridean Martinezs. The Ministry of Magic has a job hushing them up, I can tell you. Our kind have to keep putting spells on Muggles who've spotted them, to make them forget."
"So what on earths Villalba up to?" said Carolina.
When they knocked on the door of the gamekeeper's hut an hour later, they were surprised to see that all the curtains were closed. Villalba called "Who is it?" before he let them in, and then shut the door quickly behind them.
It was stifling hot inside. Even though it was such a warm day, there was a blazing fire in the grate. Villalba made them tea and offered them stoat sandwiches, which they refused.
"So -- yeh wanted to ask me somethin'?"
"Yes," said Roberto. There was no point beating around the bush. "We were wondering if you could tell us what's guarding the Sorcerer's Stone
apart from Fluffy."

Villalba frowned at him.
"0' course I cant, he said. "Number one, I don' know meself. Number two, yeh know too much already, so I wouldn' tell yeh if I could. That

Roberto knew Diego and Carolina were thinking the same as he was. If Peralta had been in on protecting the Stone, it must have been easy to find out how the other teachers had guarded it. He probably knew everything -- except, it seemed, Quirrell's spell and how to get past Fluffy.
"You're the only one who knows how to get past Fluffy. aren't you, Villalba?" said Roberto anxiously. "And you wouldn't tell anyone, would you? Not even one of the teachers?"

all in here. Keep the egg in the fire, 'cause their mothers breathe on I em, see, an' when it hatches, feed it on a bucket o' brandy mixed with chicken blood every half hour. An' see here -- how ter recognize diff'rent eggs -- what I got there's a Norwegian Ridgeback. They're rare, them."
He looked very pleased with himself, but Carolina didn't. "Villalba, you live in a wooden house," she said.
But Villalba wasn't listening. He was humming merrily as he stoked the fire.
So now they had something else to worry about: what might happen to Villalba if anyone found out he was hiding an illegal dragon in his hut. "Wonder what it's like to have a peaceful life," Diego sighed, as evening after evening they struggled through all the extra homework they were getting. Carolina had now started making study schedules for Roberto and Diego, too. It was driving them nuts.

Then, one breakfast time, Hedwig brought Roberto another note from Villalba. He had written only two words: It's hatching.

Sosa was only a few feet away and he had stopped dead to listen. How much had he heard? Roberto didn't like the look on Sosa's face at all.

The egg was lying on the table. There were deep cracks in it. Something was moving inside; a funny clicking noise was coming from it.
They all drew their chairs up to the table and watched with bated breath.
All at once there was a scraping noise and the egg split open. The baby dragon flopped onto the table. It wasn't exactly pretty; Roberto thought
it looked like a crumpled, black umbrella. Its spiny wings were huge compared to its skinny jet body, it had a long snout with wide nostrils, the stubs of horns and bulging, orange eyes.
It sneezed. A couple of sparks flew out of its snout.
"Isn't he beautiful?" Villalba murmured. He reached out a hand to stroke the dragon's head. It snapped at his fingers, showing pointed fangs.

"What's the matter?"
"Someone was lookin' through the gap in the curtains -- it's a kid -- he's runnin' back up ter the school."
Roberto bolted to the door and looked out. Even at a distance there was no mistaking him.
Sosa had seen the dragon.
Something about the smile lurking on Sosa's face during the next week made Roberto, Diego, and Carolina very nervous. They spent most of their free time in Villalba's darkened hut, trying to reason with him.
"Just let him go," Roberto urged. "Set him free."

They looked at the dragon. It had grown three times in length in just a week. Smoke kept furling out of its nostrils. Villalba hadn't been doing

They looked at one another.
"We've got the invisibility cloak," said Roberto. "It shouldn't be too difficult -- I think the cloaks big enough to cover two of us and Norbert."
It was a mark of how bad the last week had been that the other two agreed with him. Anything to get rid of Norbert -- and Sosa.
There was a hitch. By the next morning, Diego's bitten hand had swollen to twice its usual size. He didn't know whether it was safe to go to Madam Pomfrey -- would she recognize a dragon bite? By the afternoon, though, he had no choice. The cut had turned a nasty shade of green. It looked
as if Norbert's fangs were poisonous.

into a sweat.
"Midnight on Saturday!" he said in a hoarse voice. "Oh no oh no -- I've just remembered -- Charlie's letter was in that book Sosa took, he's going to know we're getting rid of Norbert."
Roberto and Carolina didn't get a chance to answer. Madam Pomfrey came over at that moment and made them leave, saying Diego needed sleep.
"It's too late to change the plan now," Roberto told Carolina. "We haven't got time to send Charlie another owl, and this could be our only chance to get rid of Norbert. We'll have to risk it. And we have got the invisibility cloak, Sosa doesn't know about that."
They found Fang, the boarhound, sitting outside with a bandaged tail when they went to tell Villalba, who opened a window to talk to them.

The baby banged its tail on the wall, making the windows rattle. Roberto and Carolina walked back to the castle feeling Saturday couldn't come quickly enough.
They would have felt sorry for Villalba when the time came for him to say good-bye to Norbert if they hadn't been so worried about what they had to do. It was a very dark, cloudy night, and they were a bit late
arriving at Villalba's hut because they'd had to wait for Peeves to get
out of their way in the entrance hall, where he'd been playing tennis against the wall. Villalba had Norbert packed and ready in a large crate.
"He's got lots o' rats an' some brandy fer the journey," said Villalba in a muffled voice. "An' I've packed his teddy bear in case he gets lonely."
From inside the crate came ripping noises that sounded to Roberto as
191
though the teddy was having his head torn off.
"Bye-bye, Norbert!" Villalba sobbed, as Roberto and Carolina covered the crate with the invisibility cloak and stepped underneath it themselves. "Mommy will never forget you!"
How they managed to get the crate back up to the castle, they never knew. Midnight ticked nearer as they heaved Norbert up the marble staircase in the entrance hall and along the dark corridors. UP another staircase, then another -- even one of Roberto's shortcuts didn't make the work much easier.
"Nearly there!" Roberto panted as they reached the corridor beneath the tallest tower.
Then a sudden movement ahead of them made them almost drop the crate. Forgetting that they were already invisible, they shrank into the
shadows, staring at the dark outlines of two people grappling with each other ten feet away. A lamp flared.
Professor Romero, in a tartan bathrobe and a hair net, had Sosa by the ear.
"Detention!" she shouted. "And twenty points from Slytherin! Wandering around in the middle of the night, how dare you --"
"You don't understand, Professor. Roberto Gonzales's coming -- he's got a dragon!"
"What utter rubbish! How dare you tell such lies! Come on -- I shall see Professor Peralta about you, Sosa!"
The steep spiral staircase up to the top of the tower seemed the easiest thing in the world after that. Not until they'd stepped out into the
cold night air did they throw off the cloak, glad to be able to breathe properly again. Carolina did a sort of jig.
"Sosa's got detention! I could sing!" "Don't," Roberto advised her.
Chuckling about Sosa, they waited, Norbert thrashing about in his crate. About ten minutes later, four broomsticks came swooping down out

of the darkness.
Charlie's friends were a cheery lot. They showed Roberto and Carolina the harness they'd rigged up, so they could suspend Norbert between them. They all helped buckle Norbert safely into it and then Roberto and Carolina shook hands with the others and thanked them very much.
At last, Norbert was going... going... gone.
They slipped back down the spiral staircase, their hearts as light as
their hands, now that Norbert was off them. No more dragon -- Sosa in detention -- what could spoil their happiness?
The answer to that was waiting at the foot of the stairs. As they stepped into the corridor, Filch's face loomed suddenly out of the darkness.
"Well, well, well," he whispered, "we are in trouble." They'd left the invisibility cloak on top of the tower.
CHAPTER FIFTEEN
THE FORIBIDDEN FOREST Things couldn't have been worse.
Filch took them down to Professor Romero's study on the first floor, where they sat and waited without saying a word to each other. Carolina was trembling. Excuses, alibis, and wild cover- up stories chased each other around Roberto's brain, each more feeble than the last. He couldn't
see how they were going to get out of trouble this time. They were cornered. How could they have been so stupid as to forget the cloak? There was no reason on earth that Professor Romero would accept for their being out of bed and creeping around the school in the dead of
night, let alone being up the tallest astronomy tower, which was out-of-bounds except for classes. Add Norbert and the invisibility cloak, and they might as well be packing their bags already.
Had Roberto thought that things couldn't have been worse? He was wrong. When Professor Romero appeared, she was leading Mauricio.
193
"Roberto!" Mauricio burst Out, the moment he saw the other two. "I was trying to find you to warn you, I heard Sosa saying he was going to catch you, he said you had a drag --"
Roberto shook his head violently to shut Mauricio up, but Professor Romero had seen. She looked more likely to breathe fire than Norbert as she towered over the three of them.
"I would never have believed it of any of you. Mr. Filch says you were up in the astronomy tower. It's one o'clock in the morning. Explain yourselves."
It was the first time Carolina had ever failed to answer a teacher's question. She was staring at her slippers, as still as a statue.
"I think I've got a good idea of what's been going on," said Professor Romero. "It doesn't take a genius to work it out. You fed Javier Sosa some cock-and-bull story about a dragon, trying to get him out of bed and into trouble. I've already caught him. I suppose you think it's funny that Silva here heard the story and believed it, too?"
Roberto caught Mauricio's eye and tried to tell him without words that this wasn't true, because Mauricio was looking stunned and hurt. Poor, blundering Mauricio -- Roberto knew what it must have cost him to try and find them in the dark, to warn them.
"I'm disgusted," said Professor Romero. "Four students out of bed in one night! I've never heard of such a thing before! You, Miss Fernandez, I thought you had more sense. As for you, Mr. Gonzales, I thought Gryffindor meant more to you than this. All three of you will receive detentions -- yes, you too, Mr. Silva, nothing gives you the right to walk around school at night, especially these days, it's very dangerous -- and fifty points will be taken from Gryffindor."
"Fifty?" Roberto gasped -- they would lose the lead, the lead he'd won in the last Quidditch match.
"Fifty points each," said Professor Romero, breathing heavily through her long, pointed nose.
"Professor -- please "You can't --"
194
"Don't tell me what I can and can't do, Gonzales. Now get back to bed, all of you. I've never been more ashamed of Gryffindor students."
A hundred and fifty points lost. That put Gryffindor in last place. In
one night, they'd ruined any chance Gryffindor had had for the house
cup. Roberto felt as though the bottom had dropped out of his stomach. How could they ever make up for this?
Roberto didn't sleep all night. He could hear Mauricio sobbing into his pillow for what seemed like hours. Roberto couldn't think of anything to say to comfort him. He knew Mauricio, like himself, was dreading the dawn. What would happen when the rest of Gryffindor found out what they'd done?
At first, Gryffindors passing the giant hourglasses that recorded the house points the next day thought there'd been a mistake. How could they suddenly have a hundred and fifty points fewer than yesterday? And then the story started to spread: Roberto Gonzales, the famous Roberto Gonzales,
their hero of two Quidditch matches, had lo st them all those points,
him and a couple of other stupid first years.
From being one of the most popular and admired people at the school, Roberto was suddenly the most hated. Even Ravenclaws and Hufflepuffs turned on him, because everyone had been longing to see Slytherin lose the house cup. Everywhere Roberto went, people pointed and didn't trouble to lower their voices as they insulted him. Slytherins, on the other
hand, clapped as he walked past them, whistling and cheering, "Thanks Gonzales, we owe you one!"
Only Diego stood by him.
"They'll all forget this in a few weeks. Pablo and Luis have lost loads of points in all the time they've been here, and people still like
them."
"They've never lost a hundred and fifty points in one go, though, have they?" said Roberto miserably.
"Well -- no," Diego admitted.
It was a bit late to repair the damage, but Roberto swore to himself not to meddle in things that weren't his business from now on. He'd had it
195
with sneaking around and spying. He felt so ashamed of himself that he went to Wood and offered to resign from the Quidditch team.
"Resign?" Wood thundered. "What good'll that do? How are we going to get any points back if we can't win at Quidditch?"
But even Quidditch had lost its fun. The rest of the team wouldn't speak to Roberto during practice, and if they had to speak about him, they called him "the Seeker."
Carolina and Mauricio were suffering, too. They didn't have as bad a time as Roberto, because they weren't as well-known, but nobody would speak to them, either. Carolina had stopped drawing attention to herself in
class, keeping her head down and working in silence.
Roberto was almost glad that the exams weren't far away. All the studying he had to do kept his mind off his misery. He, Diego, and Carolina kept to themselves, working late into the night, trying to remember the ingredients in complicated potions, learn charms and spells by heart, memorize the dates of magical discoveries and goblin rebellions....
Then, about a week before the exams were due to start, Roberto's new resolution not to interfere in anything that didn't concern him was put
to an unexpected test. Walking back from the library on his own one afternoon, he heard somebody whimpering from a classroom up ahead. As he drew closer, he heard Quirrell's voice.
"No -- no -- not again, please --"
It sounded as though someone was threatening him. Roberto moved closer. "All right -- all right --" he heard Quirrell sob.
Next second, Quirrell came hurrying out of the classroom straightening his turban. He was pale and looked as though he was about to cry. He strode out of sight; Roberto didn't think Quirrell had even noticed him. He waited until Quirrell's footsteps had disappeared, then peered into the classroom. It was empty, but a door stood ajar at the other end. Roberto was halfway toward it before he remembered what he'd promised himself about not meddling.
All the same, he'd have gambled twelve Sorcerer's Stones that Peralta had just left the room, and from what Roberto had just heard, Peralta would be
196
walking with a new spring in his step -- Quirrell seemed to have given in at last.
Roberto went back to the library, where Carolina was testing Diego on Astronomy. Roberto told them what he'd heard.
"Peralta's done it, then!" said Diego. "If Quirrell's told him how to break his Anti-Dark Force spell --"
"There's still Fluffy, though," said Carolina.
"Maybe Peralta's found out how to get past him without asking Villalba," said Diego, looking up at the thousands of books surrounding them. "I bet there's a book somewhere in here telling you how to get past a giant three-headed dog. So what do we do, Roberto?"
The light of adventure was kindling again in Diego's eyes, but Carolina answered before Roberto could.
"Go to Dominguez. That's what we should have done ages ago. If we try anything ourselves we'll be thrown out for sure."
"But we've got no proof!" said Roberto. "Quirrell's too scared to back us up. Peralta's only got to say he doesn't know how the troll got in at Halloween and that he was nowhere near the third floor -- who do you think they'll believe, him or us? It's not exactly a secret we hate him, Dominguez'll think we made it up to get him sacked. Filch wouldn't help us if his life depended on it, he's too friendly with Peralta, and the
more students get thrown out, the better, he'll think. And don't forget, we're not supposed to know about the Stone or Fluffy. That'll take a lot of explaining."
Carolina looked convinced, but Diego didn't.
"If we just do a bit of poking around --"
"No," said Roberto flatly, "we've done enough poking around."
He pulled a map of Jupiter toward him and started to learn the names of its moons.
The following morning, notes were delivered to Roberto, Carolina, and Mauricio at the breakfast table. They were all the same:

Your detention will take place at eleven o'clock tonight. Meet Mr. Filch in the entrance hall.
Professor Romero Roberto had forgotten they still had detentions to do in the furor over the points they'd lost. He half expected Carolina to complain that this was a whole night of studying lost, but she didn't
say a word. Like Roberto, she felt they deserved what they'd got.
At eleven o'clock that night, they said good-bye to Diego in the common room and went down to the entrance hall with Mauricio. Filch was already there -- and so was Sosa. Roberto had also forgotten that Sosa had gotten a detention, too.
"Follow me," said Filch, lighting a lamp and leading them outside.
I bet you'll think twice about breaking a school rule again, won't you, eh?" he said, leering at them. "Oh yes... hard work and pain are the best teachers if you ask me.... It's just a pity they let the old punishments die out... hang you by your wrists from the ceiling for a few days, I've got the chains still in my office, keep 'em well oiled in case they're ever needed.... Right, off we go, and don't think of running off, now, it'll be worse for you if you do."
They marched off across the dark grounds. Mauricio kept sniffing. Roberto wondered what their punishment was going to be. It must be something really horrible, or Filch wouldn't be sounding so delighted.
The moon was bright, but clouds scudding across it kept throwing them into darkness. Ahead, Roberto could see the lighted windows of Villalba's hut. Then they heard a distant shout.
"Is that you, Filch? Hurry up, I want ter get started."
Roberto's heart rose; if they were going to be working with Villalba it wouldn't be so bad. At this, Mauricio let out a little moan, and Sosa stopped dead in his tracks.

The forest was black and silent. A little way into it they reached a fork in the earth path, and Roberto, Carolina, and Villalba took the left path while Sosa, Mauricio, and Fang took the right.
They walked in silence, their eyes on the ground. Every now and then a ray of moonlight through the branches above lit a spot of silver-blue

Roberto saw that Villalba looked very worried.

They walked past a mossy tree stump. Roberto could hear running water; there must be a stream somewhere close by. There were still spots of unicorn blood here and there along the winding path.
"You all right, Carolina?" Villalba whispered. "Don' worry, it can't've gone far if it's this badly hurt, an' then we'll be able ter -- GET BEHIND THAT TREE!"
Villalba seized Roberto and Carolina and hoisted them off the path behind a towering oak. He pulled out an arrow and fitted it into his crossbow, raising it, ready to fire. The three of them listened. Something was slithering over dead leaves nearby: it sounded like a cloak trailing
along the ground. Villalba was squinting up the dark path, but after a few seconds, the sound faded away.

They walked more slowly, ears straining for the faintest sound. Suddenly, in a clearing ahead, something definitely moved.
"Who's there?" Villalba called. "Show yerself -- I'm armed!"
And into the clearing came -- was it a man, or a horse? To the waist, a man, with red hair and beard, but below that was a horse's gleaming chestnut body with a long, reddish tail. Roberto and Carolina's jaws dropped.

At last, a great crunching noise announced Villalba's return. Sosa, Mauricio, and Fang were with him. Villalba was fuming. Sosa, it seemed, had sneaked up behind Mauricio and grabbed him as a joke. Mauricio had panicked and sent up the sparks.

I'm sorry," Villalba added in a whisper to Roberto, "but he'll have a harder time frightenin' you, an' we've gotta get this done."
So Roberto set off into the heart of the forest with Sosa and Fang. They walked for nearly half an hour, deeper and deeper into the forest, until the path became almost impossible to follow because the trees were so thick. Roberto thought the blood seemed to be getting thicker. There were splashes on the roots of a tree, as though the poor creature had been thrashing around in pain close by. Roberto could see a clearing ahead, through the tangled branches of an ancient oak.
"Look --" he murmured, holding out his arm to stop Sosa.
Something bright white was gleaming on the ground. They inched closer.
It was the unicorn all right, and it was dead. Roberto had never seen anything so beautiful and sad. Its long, slender legs were stuck out at odd angles where it had fallen and its mane was spread pearly-white on

the dark leaves.
Roberto had taken one step toward it when a slithering sound made him freeze where he stood. A bush on the edge of the clearing quivered.... Then, out of the shadows, a hooded figure came crawling across the ground like some stalking beast. Roberto, Sosa, and Fang stood transfixed. The cloaked figure reached the unicorn, lowered its head over the wound in the animal's side, and began to drink its blood.
"AAAAAAAAAARGH!"
Sosa let out a terrible scream and bolted -- so did Fang. The hooded figure raised its head and looked right at Roberto -- unicorn blood was dribbling down its front. It got to its feet and came swiftly toward Roberto -- he couldn't move for fear.
Then a pain like he'd never felt before pierced his head; it was as though his scar were on fire. Half blinded, he staggered backward. He heard hooves behind him, galloping, and something jumped clean over Roberto, charging at the figure.
The pain in Roberto's head was so bad he fell to his knees. It took a
minute or two to pass. When he looked up, the figure had gone. A centaur was standing over him, not Diegoan or Bane; this one looked younger; he had white-blond hair and a palomino body.

Roberto didn't have a clue what was going on.
"Why's Bane so angry?" he asked. "What was that thing you saved me from, anyway?"
Firenze slowed to a walk, warned Roberto to keep his head bowed in case of low-hanging branches, but did not answer Roberto's question. They made their way through the trees in silence for so long that Roberto thought Firenze didn't want to talk to him anymore. They were passing through a particularly dense patch of trees, however, when Firenze suddenly stopped.

enough to drink something else -- something that will bring you back to full strength and power -- something that will mean you can never die. Mr. Gonzales, do you know what is hidden in the school at this very moment?"

"Can you think of nobody who has waited many years to return to power, who has clung to life, awaiting their chance?"
It was as though an iron fist had clenched suddenly around Roberto's
heart. Over the rustling of the trees, he seemed to hear once more what Villalba had told him on the night they had met: "Some say he died. Codswallop, in my opinion. Dunno if he had enough human left in him to die."
"Do you mean," Roberto croaked, "that was Vol-"
"Roberto! Roberto, are you all right?"
Carolina was running toward them down the path, Villalba puffing along
207
behind her.
"I'm fine," said Roberto, hardly knowing what he was saying. "The unicorn's dead, Villalba, it's in that clearing back there."
"This is where I leave you," Firenze murmured as Villalba hurried off to examine the unicorn. "You are safe now."
Roberto slid off his back.
"Good luck, Roberto Gonzales," said Firenze. "The planets have been read wrongly before now, even by centaurs. I hope this is one of those times."
He turned and cantered back into the depths of the forest, leaving Roberto shivering behind him.
Diego had fallen asleep in the dark common room, waiting for them to return. He shouted something about Quidditch fouls when Roberto roughly shook him awake. In a matter of seconds, though, he was wide-eyed as Roberto began to tell him and Carolina what had happened in the forest.
Roberto couldn't sit down. He paced up and down in front of the fire. He was still shaking.
"Peralta wants the stone for Salvador... and Salvador's waiting in the forest... and all this time we thought Peralta just wanted to get
rich...."
"Stop saying the name!" said Diego in a terrified whisper, as if he thought Salvador could hear them.
Roberto wasn't listening.
"Firenze saved me, but he shouldn't have done so.... Bane was furious... he was talking about interfering with what the planets say is going to happen.... They must show that Salvador's coming back.... Bane thinks Firenze should have let Salvador kill me.... I suppose that's written
in the stars as well."
"Will you stop saying the name!" Diego hissed.
"So all I've got to wait for now is Peralta to steal the Stone," Roberto

went on feverishly, "then Salvador will be able to come and finish me off... Well, I suppose Bane'll be happy."
Carolina looked very frightened, but she had a word of comfort.
"Roberto, everyone says Dominguez's the only one You-Know-Who was ever afraid of With Dominguez around, You-Know-Who won't touch you. Anyway, who says the centaurs are right? It sounds like fortune-telling to me,
and Professor Romero says that's a very imprecise branch of magic."
The sky had turned light before they stopped talking. They went to bed exhausted, their throats sore. But the night's surprises weren't over.
When Roberto pulled back his sheets, he found his invisibility cloak folded neatly underneath them. There was a note pinned to it:
Just in case.
CHAPTER SIXTEEN THROUGH THE TRAPDOOR
In years to come, Roberto would never quite remember how he had managed to get through his exams when he half expected Salvador to come bursting through the door at any moment. Yet the days crept by, and there could
be no doubt that Fluffy was still alive and well behind the locked door.
It was sweltering hot, especially in the large classroom where they did their written papers. They had been given special, new quills for the exams, which had been bewitched with an AntiCheating spell.
They had practical exams as well. Professor Flitwick called them one by one into his class to see if they could make a pineapple tapdance across
a desk. Professor Romero watched them turn a mouse into a snuffbox -- points were given for how pretty the snuffbox was, but taken away if
it had whiskers. Peralta made them all nervous, breathing down their necks while they tried to remember how to make a Forgetfulness potion.
Roberto did the best he could, trying to ignore the stabbing pains in his forehead, which had been bothering him ever since his trip into the forest. Mauricio thought Roberto had a bad case of exam nerves because Roberto couldn't sleep, but the truth was that Roberto kept being woken by
209
his old nightmare, except that it was now worse than ever because there was a hooded figure dripping blood in it.
Maybe it was because they hadn't seen what Roberto had seen in the forest, or because they didn't have scars burning on their foreheads, but Diego and Carolina didn't seem as worried about the Stone as Roberto. The idea of Salvador certainly scared them, but he didn't keep visiting them in dreams, and they were so busy with their studying they didn't have much time to fret about what Peralta or anyone else might be up to.
Their very last exam was History of Magic. One hour of answering questions about batty old wizards who'd invented selfstirring cauldrons and they'd be free, free for a whole wonderful week until their exam results came out. When the ghost of Professor Binns told them to put down their quills and roll up their parchment, Roberto couldn't help cheering with the rest.
"That was far easier than I thought it would be," said Carolina as they joined the crowds flocking out onto the sunny grounds. "I needn't have learned about the 1637 Werewolf Code of Conduct or the uprising of Elfric the Eager."
Carolina always liked to go through their exam papers afterward, but Diego said this made him feel ill, so they wandered down to the lake and
flopped under a tree. The Lopez twins and Lee Jordan were tickling the tentacles of a giant squid, which was basking in the warm shallows. "No more studying," Diego sighed happily, stretching out on the grass. "You could look more cheerful, Roberto, we've got a week before we find out how badly we've done, there's no need to worry yet."
Roberto was rubbing his forehead.
"I wish I knew what this means!" he burst out angrily. "My scar keeps hurting -- it's happened before, but never as often as this."
"Go to Madam Pomfrey," Carolina suggested.
"I'm not ill," said Roberto. "I think it's a warning... it means danger's coming...."
Diego couldn't get worked up, it was too hot.
"Roberto, relax, Carolina's right, the Stone's safe as long as
210
Dominguez's around. Anyway, we've never had any proof Peralta found out how to get past Fluffy. He nearly had his leg ripped off once, he's not
going to try it again in a hurry. And Mauricio will play Quidditch for England before Villalba lets Dominguez down."
Roberto nodded, but he couldn't shake off a lurking feeling that there was something he'd forgotten to do, something important. When he tried to explain this, Carolina said, "That's just the exams. I woke up last night and was halfway through my Transfiguration notes before I remembered we'd done that one."
Roberto was quite sure the unsettled feeling didn't have anything to do with work, though. He watched an owl flutter toward the school across the bright blue sky, a note clamped in its mouth. Villalba was the only one who ever sent him letters. Villalba would never betray Dominguez. Villalba would never tell anyone how to get past Fluffy... never... but --
Roberto suddenly jumped to his feet. "Where're you going?" said Diego sleepily.
"I've just thought of something," said Roberto. He had turned white. "We've got to go and see Villalba, now."
"Why?" panted Carolina, hurrying to keep up.
"Don't you think it's a bit odd," said Roberto, scrambling up the grassy slope, "that what Villalba wants more than anything else is a dragon, and a stranger turns up who just happens to have an egg in his pocket? How many people wander around with dragon eggs if it's against wizard law? Lucky they found Villalba, don't you think? Why didn't I see it before?"
"What are you talking about?" said Diego, but Roberto, sprinting across the grounds toward the forest, didn't answer.
Villalba was sitting in an armchair outside his house; his trousers and sleeves were rolled up, and he was shelling peas into a large bowl.

that night you won Norbert? What did the stranger you were playing cards with look like?"

"Now what do we do?" Roberto whispered.

He walked up to a black knight and put his hand out to touch the knight's horse. At once, the stone sprang to life. The horse pawed the ground and the knight turned his helmeted head to look down at Diego.
"Do we -- er -- have to join you to get across?" The black knight nodded. Diego turned to the other two.
"This needs thinking about he said. I suppose we've got to take the place of three of the black pieces...."
Roberto and Carolina stayed quiet, watching Diego think. Finally he said, "Now, don't be offended or anything, but neither of you are that good at chess --"

"Well, Roberto, you take the place of that bishop, and Carolina, YOU 90 next to him instead of that castle."

"I'm going to be a knight," said Diego.
The chessmen seemed to have been listening, because at these words a knight, a bishop, and a castle turned their backs on the white pieces and walked off the board, leaving three empty squares that Roberto, Diego, and Carolina took.
"White always plays first in chess," said Diego, peering across the board. "Yes... look..."
A white pawn had moved forward two squares.
226
Diego started to direct the black pieces. They moved silently wherever he sent them. Roberto's knees were trembling. What if they lost?
"Roberto -- move diagonally four squares to the right."
Their first real shock came when their other knight was taken. The white queen smashed him to the floor and dragged him off the board, where he lay quite still, facedown.

Every time one of their men was lost, the white pieces showed no mercy. Soon there was a huddle of limp black players slumped along the wall. Twice, Diego only just noticed in time that Roberto and Carolina were in danger. He himself darted around the board, taking almost as many white pieces as they had lost black ones.
"We're nearly there," he muttered suddenly. "Let me think let me think..."
The white queen turned her blank face toward him.

"What if he's --?"

Roberto pushed it open.

He pulled open the next door, both of them hardly daring to look at what came next - but there was nothing very frightening in here, just a table with seven differently shaped bottles standing on it in a line.
228
"Peralta's," said Roberto. "What do we have to do?"

Danger lies before you, while safety lies behind,
Two of us will help you, which ever you would find,
One among us seven will let you move ahead,
Another will transport the drinker back instead,
Two among our number hold only nettle wine,
Three of us are killers, waiting bidden in line.
Paulaose, unless you wish to stay here forevermore,
To help you in your choice, we give you these clues four: First, however slyly the poison tries to hide

Neither dwarf nor giant holds death in their insides;
Fourth, the second left and the second on the right
Are twins once you taste them, though different at first sight.

Carolina let out a great sigh and Roberto, amazed, saw that she was smiling, the very last thing he felt like doing.

Carolina read the paper several times. Then she walked up and down the line of bottles, muttering to herself and pointing at them. At last, she clapped her hands.

Roberto looked at the tiny bottle.

THE MAN WITH TWO FACES
It was Quirrell.

Quirrell smiled. His face wasn't twitching at all.

"It's -- all -- my -- ruddy -- fault!" he sobbed, his face in his hands. I told the evil git how ter get past Fluffy! I told him! It was the only

thing he didn't know, an' I told him! Yeh could've died! All fer a dragon egg! I'll never drink again! I should be chucked out an' made ter live as a Muggle!"
"Villalba!" said Roberto, shocked to see Villalba shaking with grief and remorse, great tears leaking down into his beard. "Villalba, he'd have found out somehow, this is Salvador we're talking about, he'd have found out even if you hadn't told him."
"Yeh could've died!" sobbed Villalba. "An' don' say the name!"
"SALVADOR!" Roberto bellowed, and Villalba was so shocked, he stopped crying. "I've met him and I'm calling him by his name. Please cheer up, Villalba, we saved the Stone, it's gone, he can't use it. Have a Paulacolate Frog, I've got loads...."
Villalba wiped his nose on the back of his hand and said, "That reminds me. I've got yeh a present."
"It's not a stoat sandwich, is it?" said Roberto anxiously, and at last Villalba gave a weak chuckle. "Nah. Dominguez gave me the day off yesterday ter fix it. 'Course, he shoulda sacked me instead -- anyway, got yeh this..."
It seemed to be a handsome, leather-covered book. Roberto opened it curiously. It was full of wizard photographs. Smiling and waving at him from every page were his mother and father.
"Sent owls off ter all yer parents' old school friends, askin' fer photos... knew yeh didn' have any... d'yeh like it?"
Roberto couldn't speak, but Villalba understood.
Roberto made his way down to the end-of-year feast alone that night. He had been held up by Madam Pomfrey's fussing about, insisting on giving him one last checkup, so the Great Hall was already full. It was decked out in the Slytherin colors of green and silver to celebrate Slytherin's winning the house cup for the seventh year in a row. A huge banner showing the Slytherin serpent covered the wall behind the High Table.
When Roberto walked in there was a sudden hush, and then everybody started talking loudly at once. He slipped into a seat between Diego and Carolina
at the Gryffindor table and tried to ignore the fact that people were
245
standing up to look at him.
Fortunately, Dominguez arrived moments later. The babble died away.
"Another year gone!" Dominguez said cheerfully. "And I must trouble you with an old man's wheezing waffle before we sink our teeth into our delicious feast. What a year it has been! Hopefully your heads are all a little fuller than they were... you have the whole summer ahead to get
them nice and empty before next year starts....
"Now, as I understand it, the house cup here needs awarding, and the points stand thus: In fourth place, Gryffindor, with three hundred and twelve points; in third, Hufflepuff, with three hundred and fifty-two; Ravenclaw has four hundred and twenty-six and Slytherin, four hundred and seventy- two."
A storm of cheering and stamping broke out from the Slytherin table. Roberto could see Javier Sosa banging his goblet on the table. It was a sickening sight.
"Yes, Yes, well done, Slytherin," said Dominguez. "However, recent events must be taken into account."
The room went very still. The Slytherins' smiles faded a little.
"Ahem," said Dominguez. "I have a few last-minute points to dish out. Let me see. Yes...
"First -- to Mr. Diegoald Lopez..."
Diego went purple in the face; he looked like a radish with a bad sunburn.
"...for the best-played game of chess Hogwarts has seen in many years, I award Gryffindor house fifty points."
Gryffindor cheers nearly raised the bewitched ceiling; the stars overhead seemed to quiver. Miguel could be heard telling the other prefects, "My brother, you know! My youngest brother! Got past Romero's giant chess set!"
At last there was silence again.
"Second -- to Miss Carolina Fernandez... for the use of cool logic in the
246
face of fire, I award Gryffindor house fifty points."
Carolina buried her face in her arms; Roberto strongly suspected she had burst into tears. Gryffindors up and down the table were beside themselves -- they were a hundred points up. "Third -- to Mr. Roberto Gonzales..." said Dominguez. The room went deadly quiet for pure nerve and outstanding courage, I award Gryffindor house sixty points."
The din was deafening. Those who could add up while yelling themselves hoarse knew that Gryffindor now had four hundred and seventy-two points -- exactly the same as Slytherin. They had tied for the house cup -- if
only Dominguez had given Roberto just one more point.
Dominguez raised his hand. The room gradually fell silent.
"There are all kinds of courage," said Dominguez, smiling. "It takes a great deal of bravery to stand up to our enemies, but just as much to stand up to our friends. I therefore award ten points to Mr. Mauricio Silva."
Someone standing outside the Great Hall might well have thought some sort of explosion had taken place, so loud was the noise that erupted
from the Gryffindor table. Roberto, Diego, and Carolina stood up to yell and cheer as Mauricio, white with shock, disappeared under a pile of people hugging him. He had never won so much as a point for Gryffindor before. Roberto, still cheering, nudged Diego in the ribs and pointed at Sosa, who couldn't have looked more stunned and horrified if he'd just had the Body-Bind Curse put on him.
"Which means, Dominguez called over the storm of applause, for even Ravenclaw and Hufflepuff were celebrating the downfall of Slytherin, "we need a little change of decoration."
He clapped his hands. In an instant, the green hangings became scarlet and the silver became gold; the huge Slytherin serpent vanished and a towering Gryffindor lion took its place. Peralta was shaking Professor Romero's hand, with a horrible, forced smile. He caught Roberto's eye and Roberto knew at once that Peralta's feelings toward him hadn't changed one jot. This didn't worry Roberto. It seemed as though life would be back to normal next year, or as normal as it ever was at Hogwarts.
It was the best evening of Roberto's life, better than winning at Quidditch, or Christmas, or knocking out mountain trolls... he would
247
never, ever forget tonight.
Roberto had almost forgotten that the exam results were still to come, but come they did. To their great surprise, both he and Diego passed with good marks; Carolina, of course, had the best grades of the first years. Even Mauricio scraped through, his good Herbology mark making up for his abysmal Potions one. They had hoped that Goyle, who was almost as stupid as he was mean, might be thrown out, but he had passed, too. It was a shame, but as Diego said, you couldn't have everything in life.
And suddenly, their wardrobes were empty, their trunks were packed, Mauricio's toad was found lurking in a corner of the toilets; notes were handed out to all students, warning them not to use magic over the holidays ("I always hope they'll forget to give us these," said Pablo Lopez sadly); Villalba was there to take them down to the fleet of boats that sailed across the lake; they were boarding the Hogwarts Express; talking and laughing as the countryside became greener and tidier; eating Bettie Bott's Every Flavor Beans as they sped past Muggle towns; pulling off their wizard robes and putting on jackets and coats; pulling into platform nine and three-quarters at King's Cross Station.
It took quite a while for them all to get off the platform. A wizened old guard was up by the ticket barrier, letting them go through the gate in twos and threes so they didn't attract attention by all bursting out
of a solid wall at once and alarming the Muggles.
"You must come and stay this summer," said Diego, "both of you -- I'll send you an owl."
"Thanks," said Roberto, "I'll need something to look forward to." People jostled them as they moved forward toward the gateway back to the Muggle world. Some of them called:
"Bye, Roberto!"
"See you, Gonzales!"
"Still famous," said Diego, grinning at him.
"Not where I'm going, I promise you," said Roberto.
He, Diego, and Carolina passed through the gateway together. "There he is, Mom, there he is, look!"
248
It was Martina Lopez, Diego's younger sister, but she wasn't pointing at Diego.
"Roberto Gonzales!" she squealed. "Look, Mom! I can see "Be quiet, Martina, and it's rude to point."
Mrs. Lopez smiled down at them.
"Busy year?" she said.
"Very," said Roberto. "Thanks for the fudge and the sweater, Mrs. Lopez."
"Oh, it was nothing, dear." "Ready, are you?"
It was Uncle Francisco, still purple-faced, still mustached, still looking furious at the nerve of Roberto, carrying an owl in a cage in a station full of ordinary people. Behind him stood Aunt Beatriz and Leonardo, looking terrified at the very sight of Roberto.
"You must be Roberto's family!" said Mrs. Lopez.
"In a manner of speaking," said Uncle Francisco. "Hurry up, boy, we haven't got all day." He walked away.
Roberto hung back for a last word with Diego and Carolina.
"See you over the summer, then."
"Hope you have -- er -- a good holiday," said Carolina, looking uncertainly after Uncle Francisco, shocked that anyone could be so unpleasant.
"Oh, I will," said Roberto, and they were surprised at the grin that was spreading over his face. "They don't know we're not allowed to use magic at home. I'm going to have a lot of fun with Leonardo this summer...."
THE END
